  • For inability to straighten the waist, feeling heavy as if burdened by stones: Use four taels each of red poria and white atractylodes, three taels of roasted licorice, and two taels of dried ginger, decocted in water and taken in five qian doses.
  • For belt fire (a type of pain): Grind fine mud from white eels and apply with sesame oil. Another method is to burn feathers from pheasants and geese to ash and mix with sesame oil for application.
  • For sudden lower back pain: Grind fennel with red yeast rice, mix it well, and take with warm liquor. Another method is to grind fennel root and take with fine wine for immediate relief.
  • For any lower back pain: Use four taels of fresh ginger, extract the natural juice and slightly reduce it to a paste, then apply to the affected area and wrap the foot. Before applying the paste, one should slightly intoxicate themselves, then apply the paste to the affected area. When the paste is on the skin, it generates unbearable heat for a short while; intoxication induces deep sleep, thus one may not feel the heat.
  • For lower back pain: Calcine magnetite in vinegar nine times to make a powder, form into pills with water, or it can be added to kidney tonics, which is beneficial for lumbar weakness due to kidney deficiency.[102p]

　　腰痛膝冷：菟丝子酒煮作末，温酒下二钱。
　　腰痛：地黄花为末，酒服方寸匕。
　　又方：菟丝末二两，杜仲蜜炙末一两，山药末酒煮为糊作丸，酒下五七十丸，名固阳丹。
　　蛇缠疮：用雄黄研为末，以酢调涂，仍用酒调服。凡为蛇伤，及蜂虿、蜈蚣、毒虫、颠犬所伤，皆可用之。【《证治准绳》】
　　腰痛脚弱：石斛煮服、末服、浸酒服，皆佳。 【《本草》，下同】
　　腰脊痛：蒺藜子为末蜜丸服，或作末和酒服，并佳。
　　腰痛：肉苁蓉作丸服之。
　　又方：续断煮服，末服并佳。

　　腰痛：萆薢酒浸服之。
　　又方：萆薢三两，杜仲一两，捣为末，空心酒服二钱，禁食牛肉。　　又方：威灵仙细末二钱，猪腰子一只，批药在内，湿纸裹煨熟，早晨细嚼，热酒下。 【《纲目》】　　又方：威灵仙酒浸为末，面糊和丸梧子大，酒下八十丸至百丸，大便下青脓。 【《本草》，下同】[103p]

Low back pain and cold knees: Boil dodder seeds in wine and grind into a powder; take two qian with warm wine.

Low back pain: Grind Rehmannia flower into a powder and take it with wine, about the size of a thumb.

Another formula: Two liang of dodder powder, one liang of honey-roasted Eucommia powder, powdered yam, and boil with wine to form a paste to make pills; take five to seventy pills with wine, named Guyang Dan.

For snake bites: Grind realgar into a powder, mix with vinegar to apply, and also mix with wine to take. This works for injuries from snakes, bees, wasps, centipedes, venomous insects, and mad dogs.

Low back pain and weak legs: Take Stone Orchid in boiled, powdered, or wine-soaked form, all are good.

Spinal pain: Grind spiny restharrow seeds into a powder and form honey pills, or mix powder with wine, both are effective.

For low back pain: Take flesh of cistanche in pill form.

Another formula: Steep Sichuan tearwort and take in boiled or powdered form, both are good.

For low back pain: Soak Polygala in wine and take it.

Another formula: Three liang of Polygala, one liang of Eucommia, grind into a powder, take two qian with empty stomach and wine, avoiding beef.

Another formula: Two qian of finely powdered Weilingxian, one pig’s kidney, apply the medicine inside, wrap in wet paper, and steam until cooked; chew finely in the morning and wash down with hot wine.

Another formula: Soak Weilingxian in wine to make a fine powder, mix with flour to form pills the size of walnuts, take eighty to a hundred pills with wine, causing green pus in stool.[103p]

　　腰痛：五加皮细銼，酒浸服之。

　　肾虚腰痛：童便二盏，好酒一盏，猪腰子一对，盛磁缸，黄泥封口，日晚以慢火养熟至中夜，待五更初，以火温之，发瓶饮酒食腰子。此以血养血，绝胜金石草木之药。【《入门》，下同】
　　虚损腰痛：取胡桃肉和杜仲茴香浸酒，空心服。
　　腰脊痛：薏苡仁为末，煮粥空心服。
　　　　针灸

　　《素问》曰：脾热病者，热争则腰痛不可用俯仰，腹满泄，两颔痛。甲乙甚，戊己大汗。气逆则甲乙死。刺足太阴、阳明。肾热病者，先腰痛胻酸，苦渴数饮身热。戊己甚，壬癸大汗．气逆则戊己死。刺足少阴、太阳。　　足太阳之疟，令人腰痛头重，寒从背起，刺郄中出血。　　足厥阴之疟，令人腰痛少腹满，小便不利，刺足厥阴。　　肾疟者，令人洒洒寒，腰脊痛宛转，刺足太阳、少阴。　　先腰脊痛者，先刺郄中出血。[104p]

Lower back pain: Use finely shredded Wu Jia Pi, soak in wine and take it.

Kidney deficiency back pain: Two cups of young urine, one cup of good wine, a pair of pig kidneys, placed in a ceramic jar, sealed with yellow clay. Slowly cook over low heat until midnight, then warm it with fire at dawn and drink the wine and eat the kidneys. This nourishes blood with blood, far surpassing the effects of metals, stones, and herbs.

Deficiency-related back pain: Take walnut meat, mix with Eucommia bark and fennel, soak in wine, and consume on an empty stomach.

Spinal pain: Grind Coix seeds into powder, cook into porridge, and eat on an empty stomach.

Acupuncture

The "Suwen" states: For diseases caused by spleen heat, heat causing back pain makes it impossible to bend or stretch; there is abdominal fullness and diarrhea, pain in both jaws. Severe in the Jia and Yi, major sweating in Wu and Ji. If qi reverses, it can lead to Jia and Yi's death. Puncture the Foot Taiyin and Yangming points.

For kidney heat disease: First, there is back pain and sourness in the legs, bitter thirst, frequent drinking, and feeling hot. Severe in Wu and Ji, major sweating in Ren and Gui. If qi reverses, it results in Wu and Ji's death. Puncture the Foot Shaoyin and Taiyang points.

In the case of foot Taiyang malaria, it causes back pain and heaviness in the head, cold rising from the back; puncture the Xi point to induce bleeding.

In the case of foot Jueyin malaria, it causes lower back pain, fullness in the lower abdomen, and difficulty urinating; puncture the Foot Jueyin point.

For kidney malaria, it results in cold chills, twisting pain in the lower back; puncture the Foot Taiyang and Shaoyin points.

For prior lower back and spinal pain, first puncture the Xi point to induce bleeding.[104p]

　　足太阳脉，令人腰痛，引项脊尻背如重状，刺其郄中太阳正经出血。春无见血。　　少阳令人腰痛，如以针刺其皮中，循循不可以俯仰，不可以顾，刺少阳成骨之端出血。成骨在膝外廉之骨独起者。夏无见血。　　阳明令人腰痛，不可以顾，顾如有见者善悲，刺阳明于胻前三痏，上下和之，出血。秋无见血。　　足太阴令人腰痛，痛引脊内廉，刺少阴于内踝上二胻。春无见血，出血太多，不可复也。　　厥阴之脉，令人腰痛，腰中如张弓弩弦，刺厥阴之脉，在腨踵鱼腹之外，循循累累然，乃刺之。其病令人善言，默默然不慧，刺之三痏。　　解脉令人腰痛，痛引肩，目(目巟)(目巟)然，时遗溲，刺解脉在膝筋肉分间，郄外廉之横脉出血，血变而止。[105p]

The foot Taiyang channel causes pain in the lower back, leading to a feeling of heaviness in the waist and spine, as if burdened. Bloodletting at its acupoint can help, but not in spring. The Shaoyang channel also causes lower back pain, akin to being pricked by needles under the skin, making it difficult to bend or look back. Bloodletting at the endpoint of the bone associated with the Shaoyang channel can help, but not in summer. The Yangming channel results in lower back pain, making it hard to look back; if one does, it’s as if they see something sorrowful. Bloodletting at the acupoint three finger widths above the knee can be effective, but not in autumn. The foot Taiyin channel causes lower back pain that radiates from the inner spine; bloodletting at the acupoint two finger widths above the inner ankle can help, but should not be excessive in spring. The Jueyin channel causes lower back pain, feeling like drawing a bowstring. Bloodletting at the outside of the heel and along the meridian can be helpful. This condition may make one loquacious and less wise, and bloodletting at three finger widths can assist. The Jie channel induces lower back pain that radiates to the shoulders, accompanied by spontaneous urination. Bloodletting at the muscular separation in the knee area can help, stopping the blood flow once it changes.[105p]

　　解脉，令人腰痛，如引带长，如折腰状，善恐，刺解脉在郄中结络如黍米，刺之血射以黑，见赤血而已。　　同阴之脉，令人腰痛，痛如小锤居其中，怫然肿，刺同阴之脉在外踝上绝骨之端，为三痏。　　阳维之脉，令人腰痛，痛上怫然肿，刺阳维之脉，脉与太阳合踹下间去地一尺所。　　衡络之脉，令人腰痛，不可以俯仰，仰则恐仆，得之举重伤腰，衡络绝，恶血归之，刺之在郄阳筋之间，上郄数寸横居，为二痏。　　会阴之脉，令人腰痛，痛上漯漯然汗出，汗干令人欲饮，饮已欲走。刺直阳之脉上三痏，在蹺上郄下五寸横居，视其盛者出血。　　飞阳之脉，令人腰痛，痛止怫怫然，甚则悲以恐。刺飞阳之脉，在内踝上五寸，少阴之前与阴维之会。　　昌阳之脉，令人腰痛，痛引膺，目(目巟)(目巟)然，甚则反折，舌卷不能言。刺内筋为二痏，在内踝上大筋前，太阴后上踝二寸所。[106p]

The pulse of the Jie major point causes lower back pain, feeling like pulling a long belt or bending at the waist, characterized by a sense of fear. When needled at the intersection in the depression like millet, the blood that flows is black, only red blood is observed.

The pulse of the Tongyin causes lower back pain, resembling the sensation of a small hammer inside, swollen and painful. Needle the Tongyin pulse at the end of the bone above the outer ankle, aiming for three points.

The pulse of the Yangwei causes lower back pain, accompanied by swelling and pain above. Needle the Yangwei pulse at a location one foot below where it meets the Taiyang.

The pulse of the Hengluo causes lower back pain, making it difficult to bend or look up; looking up causes fear of falling. Caused by an injury from lifting heavy things, needle this at the space between the Yang tendons in the hollow, two inches above the point.

The pulse of the Huiyin causes lower back pain, with a saying of a gushing sweat that makes one want to drink; once drinking, there’s a desire to flee. Needle three points at the Jizhong, five inches below the hollow at a horizontal position, observing swelling for blood flow.

The pulse of Feiyang causes lower back pain, resulting in a dull sensation; severe cases cause sadness and fear. Needle the Feiyang pulse five inches above the inner ankle, located in front of the Shaoyin and where it meets the Yinwei.

The pulse of Changyang causes lower back pain, radiating to the chest; in extreme cases, this causes reversal, leading to a tongue that cannot speak. Needle at two points at the inner tendons, located two inches above the inner ankle in front of the major tendon, behind the Taiyin.[106p]

　　散脉，令人腰痛而热，热甚生烦，腰下如有横木居其中，甚则遗溲。刺散脉在膝骨肉分间，络外廉束脉，为三痏。　　肉里之脉，令人腰痛不可以咳，咳则筋缩急。刺肉里之脉为二痏，在太阳之外，少阳绝骨之后。　　腰痛挟脊而痛，至头八八然，目(目巟)(目巟)欲僵仆，刺足太阳郄中出血。　　腰痛上寒，刺足太阳、阳明；上热，刺足厥阴；不可以俯仰，刺足少阳；中热而喘，刺足少阴，刺郄中出血。　　腰痛上寒不可顾，刺足阳明；上热，刺足太阴；中热而喘，刺足少阴；大便难，刺足少阴；少腹满，刺足厥阴；如折不可以俛仰，不可举，刺足太阳；引脊内廉，刺足少阴。　　腰痛引少腹控(月少)，不可以仰，刺腰尻交者两踝胂上，以月生死为痏数，发针立已，左取右，右取左。[107p]

Scattered pulse causes pain and heat in the lower back; excessive heat leads to restlessness, as if a horizontal log is lodged in the lower back, and in severe cases, it results in incontinence. Needle the scattered pulse between the flesh of the knee bone, outside the channel, to treat three conditions.

The pulse within the flesh causes lower back pain that prevents coughing; if one coughs, the tendons contract and become tight. Needle the pulse within the flesh for two conditions, located outside the taiyang, behind the shaoyang’s vertex.

If the lower back pain radiates to the spine and leads to a feeling of heaviness in the head, with the eyes feeling rigid and fainting, needle the point at the outer aspect of the foot’s taiyang channel to promote bleeding.

If the lower back pain is cold in nature, needle the foot's yangming; if it is hot, needle the foot's jueyin; if it is difficult to bend or straighten, needle the foot's shaoyang; for heat in the middle and shortness of breath, needle the foot's shaoyin, also promote bleeding at the corresponding point.

If the lower back pain is accompanied by upper cold, do not look back; needle the foot's yangming; if it is hot above, needle the foot's taiyin; for middle heat and shortness of breath, needle the foot's shaoyin; if there is difficulty in bowel movement, needle the foot's shaoyin; for fullness in the lower abdomen, needle the foot's jueyin; if there is a feeling like it is breaking and cannot bend or straighten, needle the foot's taiyang. When the pain radiates to the lower abdomen, not allowing one to look up, needle the lower back and the two points near the ankles; consider the phases of the moon as conditions, inserting the needle and establishing it firmly, taking from the left for the right and from the right for the left.[107p]

　　腰痛不可以转摇，急引阴卵，刺八髎与痛上，八髎在腰尻分间。　　《灵枢经》曰：小肠病者，小腹痛，腰脊控睾而痛，时窘之后，当耳前热；若寒甚，若独肩上热甚，及手小指次指之间热，若脉陷者，此其候也，手太阳病也，取之巨虚下廉。　　病在上者，下取之；病在下者，高取之。病在头者，取之足；病在腰者，取之腘。　　足少阴之别，名曰大锺，别走太阳。其别者并经上走于心包下，外贯腰脊。其病气逆则烦闷，实则闭癃，虚则腰痛，取之所别也。　　邪在肾，则病骨痛阴痹，阴痹者按之而不得，腹胀腰痛，大便难，肩背颈项痛时眩，取之涌泉、昆仑，视有血者尽取之。　　厥头痛项先痛，腰脊为应，先取天柱，后取足太阳。　　厥挟脊而痛至顶，头沉沉然，目(目巟)(目巟)然，腰脊强，取足太阳腘中血络。　　心痛引腰脊，欲呕，取足少阴。[108p]

Lower back pain should not be moved or shaken; urgently draw from the Yin and ovarian points, and needle the eight sacral points associated with the pain, which are located between the lower back and buttocks. The "Spiritual Axis Classic" says: for small intestine diseases, there is pain in the lower abdomen, and the pain radiates to the lower back and controls the testicles. After that, there may be heat in front of the ears; if it is severe cold, there will be more heat in the shoulder and between the little finger and the next finger. If the pulse is deep, this is the indication for the hand's Taiyang disease, and one should treat the position below the giant void point.

For diseases located above, treat below; for those below, treat high. For diseases in the head, treat the feet; for those in the lower back, treat the knee pits. The branch of the foot Shaoyin is called the Great Bell, it connects to the Taiyang. Its branch travels upward along the channels to the pericardium below and outward through the lower back spine. If the pathogenic Qi is counter-flowing, it causes agitation; if it is real, it leads to retention, and if it is deficient, it results in lower back pain, which is treated at its branch.

If the evil is in the kidneys, it causes bone pain and Yin obstruction, the latter of which cannot be pressed upon. Symptoms include abdominal bloating, lower back pain, difficulty in bowel movements, and shoulder, back, and neck pain accompanied by dizziness; treat the Yongquan and Kunlun points, particularly if there is blood present.

For a type of headache preceded by neck pain, the lower back responds; first treat the Tianzhu point, then the foot Taiyang. For acute pain along the spine reaching to the top, with a heavy sensation in the head and eyes cloudy, accompanied by stiffness in the lower back and spine, treat the blood collaterals in the knee pits of the foot Taiyang. For heart pain radiating to the lower back with a desire to vomit, treat the foot Shaoyin.[108p]

　　肾气盛则梦腰脊两解不属，凡此盛者，至而泻之，立已。　　腰尻以下应冬至，其日壬子。凡此者善候八正所在之处，所主左右上下身体有痈肿者，欲治之，无以其所直之日渍治之，是谓天忌日也。　　《甲乙经》曰：腰痛上寒，实则脊急强，长强主之。　　少腹痛，控睾引腰脊，疝痛上冲心，腰脊强，溺黄赤口干，小肠俞主之。　　腰脊痛强引背少腹，俯仰难，不得仰息，脚痿重，尻不举，溺赤，腰以下至足清不仁，不可以坐起，膀胱俞主之。　　腰痛不可以俯仰，中膂内俞主之。[109p]

When the kidney's energy is strong, one dreams of the waist and spine being unbounded. In such cases, it should be released when it arrives, and it will establish itself. The lower back should be attended to during the winter solstice, particularly on the day of Renzi. In all such matters, it is important to observe the positions of the eight correct places; if there are swellings or sores in the body, one should not treat them on their direct day, for that is called an unfavorable day.

The "Jia Yi Jing" states: A cold upper back with waist pain signifies a strong spine; treat it accordingly. If there is pain in the lower abdomen pulling on the testicles and the waist and spine, this may indicate a hernia causing discomfort in the heart, with a strong waist and spine, yellow and red urination, and dry mouth, which is governed by the Small Intestine Meridian.

Pain in the waist and spine may lead to discomfort in the lower abdomen and difficulty in bending or looking up, making breathing hard, with heavy legs, an inability to lift the buttocks, red urination, and a lack of feeling from the waist down to the feet. One cannot sit up; this is governed by the Bladder Meridian.

The waist pain does not permit bending or looking up and is governed by the Zhong Liu and Neiguan Meridians.[109p]

　　腰足痛而清，善偃睾跳拳，上髎主之。　　腰痛怏怏不可以俯仰，腰以下至足不仁，入脊腰背寒，次髎主之。先取缺盆，后取尾骶与八髎。　　腰痛大便难，飧泄，腰尻中寒，中髎主之。　　腰痛脊急，胁中满，小腹坚急，志室主之。　　腰脊痛恶风，少腹满坚，癃闭下重，不得小便，胞肓主之。　　腰痛骶寒俯仰急难，阴痛下重，不得小便，秩边主之。　　腰痛控睾小腹及股，卒俯不得仰，刺气街。　　腰痛不得转侧，章门主之。[110p]

When there is pain in the lower back and legs, and when the condition is clear, one should press on Yaoyao and Tiaoqian (points), with Shangjiao being the main focus.

If there is persistent lower back pain making it difficult to bend or look up, and numbness from the lower back to the feet, with coldness along the spine and back, then focusing on Cijiao is advised. First, target Quenpen, then the sacrum and the eight Jiao points.

For lower back pain accompanied by difficulty in bowel movements and diarrhea, with coldness in the lower region, focus on Zhongjiao.

In cases of acute lower back pain, with fullness in the sides and hardness in the lower abdomen, Zhishi should be addressed.

For lower back pain that is aggravated by wind, with a full and firm lower abdomen, and issues related to urination, focus on Baohuang.

If lower back pain is cold, difficult to bend or look up, with heavy lower abdominal discomfort and difficulty urinating, then Zhibian should be the focus.

When there is pain in the lower back affecting the lower abdomen and thighs, causing an inability to bend or look up, stimulate the Qi Jie point.

For lower back pain that prevents turning or shifting sides, the main focus should be on Zhangmen.[110p]

　　腰痛不可以久立俯仰，京门及行间主之。　　腰腹少腹痛，下髎主之。
　　肾腰痛不可俯仰，阴陵泉主之。
　　腰痛少腹满，小便不利如癃状，羸瘦意恐惧气不足，腹中怏怏，太冲主之。　　腰痛少腹痛，阴包主之。
　　腰痛大便难，涌泉主之。
　　腰脊相引如解，实则闭癃，凄凄，腰脊痛宛转，目循循，嗜卧，口中热，虚则腰痛寒厥，烦心闷，大锺主之。　　腰痛引脊内廉，复溜主之。春无见血，若太多，虚不可复，是前足少阴痛也。　　腰痛不能举足，少坐若下车踬地，胫中矫矫然，申脉主之。　　腰痛如小锤居其中，怫然肿痛，不可以咳，咳则筋缩急，诸节痛，上下无常寒热，阳辅主之。　　腰痛不可举足，跟中踝后痛，脚痿，仆参主之。　　腰痛挟脊至头八八然，目(目巟)(目巟)，委中主之。[111p]

Lower back pain should not be prolonged with standing or bending; the area around the Jing Men and the spaces in between govern this.

Pain in the lower back and abdomen indicates issues in the lower back and the lower abdomen.

Kidney-related back pain should not be bent; the Yin Ling Quan governs this.

If there is back pain with fullness in the lower abdomen and difficulty urinating resembling urinary retention, along with emaciation and anxiety due to insufficient energy, and a feeling of discomfort in the abdomen, the Tai Chong governs this. If there is lower back pain and lower abdominal pain, the Yin Bao governs this.

For back pain accompanied by constipation, the Yong Quan governs this.

When back and spine pain radiates, but is actually due to urinary retention, with deep discomfort, the back and spine ache consistently, and there is an inclination to lie down, accompanied by a warm mouth, if there is a deficiency causing back pain with cold limbs, agitation, and depression, the Da Zhong governs this.

If there is back pain radiating to the inner side of the spine, the Fu Liu governs this. In spring, if there is no bleeding, but if excessive, deficiency should not be restored, as this signifies pain in the lesser yin.

When back pain prevents raising the feet, and sitting feels as though one may fall to the ground, the shins feel stiff, the Shen Mai governs this.

If the back pain feels like a small hammer inside, with swelling and pain that prevents coughing—coughing makes the muscles tense painfully, with varying sensations of hot and cold, the Yang Fu governs this.

With back pain that impedes raising the feet, pain in the back of the heel, or weakness in the legs, the Pu Shen governs this.

Finally, if back pain radiates to the head in a severe manner, accompanied by visual disturbances, the Wei Zhong governs this.[111p]

是前刺足太阳郄中出血者。　　腰痛得俯不得仰，仰则恐仆，得之举重，恶血归之，殷门主之。是前衡络之脉腰痛者。　　腰脊痛，尻脊股臀阴寒大痛，虚则血动，实则并热，痛痔，痛尻，脽中肿，大便直出，承扶主之。　　《千金方》曰：腰背痛，宜针决膝腰勾画中青赤络脉，出血便瘥。　　腰痛不得俯仰者，令患人正立，以竹拄地，度至脐断竹，乃以度之背脊，灸竹上头处，随年壮灸讫，藏竹勿令人得知。　　腰痛，灸脚跟上横文中白肉际十壮，良。　　又灸足巨阳七壮，巨阳在外踝下。[112p]

This text discusses the treatment of lower back pain and related symptoms using acupuncture and moxibustion. It describes conditions where the patient cannot bend forward or backward without fear of collapsing, experiences pain in the waist and buttocks, or has issues such as hemorrhoids and other related symptoms. It suggests specific acupuncture points and techniques for treating these issues. For those unable to bend, the patient should stand upright, supported by a bamboo pole, and specific points on the back should be treated with moxibustion without revealing the method to others. The text also mentions treating specific points on the feet to alleviate the pain effectively.[112p]

　　又灸腰目髎七壮，在尻上约左右是。　　又灸八髎，及外踝上骨约中。
　　腰卒痛，灸穷骨上一寸七壮，左右一寸各灸七壮。　　五脏六腑，心腹满，腰背疼，饮食吐逆，寒热往来，小便不利，羸瘦少气，灸三焦俞，随年壮。　　腹疾腰痛，膀胱寒，澼饮注下，灸下极俞，随年壮。　　劳冷气逆，腰臗冷痹，脚屈伸难，灸阳蹺一百壮，在外踝下容爪。　　腰背不便，转筋急痹筋挛，灸第二十一椎，随年壮。　　神道、谷中、腰俞、长强、大杼、膈关、水分、脾俞、小肠俞、膀胱俞，主腰脊急强。　　腰俞、膀胱俞、长强、气冲、上髎、下髎、居髎，主腰痛。　　志门、京门，主腰痛脊急。[113p]

Additionally, apply moxibustion to the lumbar region and the yaoli (lower back) at seven locations, located about one fist's breadth from the left and right sides of the sacrum. Also, apply moxibustion to the eight yaos and to the bones above the outer ankles at the center.

For sudden lower back pain, apply moxibustion one cun (an inch) above the tailbone at seven locations, and at seven locations on each side, one cun apart. For issues concerning the five organs and six hollow organs, such as fullness in the chest and abdomen, back pain, vomiting and regurgitation after eating, alternating chills and fever, difficulty in urination, emaciation with shortness of breath, apply moxibustion to the Sanjiao point, adjusting based on yearly changes.

For abdominal diseases and lower back pain due to cold in the bladder, causing dripping or despondent drinking, apply moxibustion to the lower jiao point, adjusting based on yearly changes. For exhausting cold leading to reversed qi, with cold and numbness in the lower back and difficulty bending or stretching the legs, apply moxibustion to the Yangqiao point with one hundred locations below the ankle where the toe can fit.

For lower back and spinal discomfort, with cramping and tightness in the muscles, apply moxibustion to the twenty-first vertebra, adjusting based on yearly changes. The points that govern acute pain in the lower back and spine include Shendao (Spirit Path), Guxiong (Valley Center), Yaoyu, Changqiang (Long Strong), Dazhu (Great Anchor), Ge Guan (Diaphragm Gate), Shuifen (Water Portion), Pishu (Spleen Back), Xiaochangshu (Small Intestine Back), and Pangguangshu (Bladder Back).

The Yaoyu, Pangguangshu, Changqiang, Qichong (Qi Surge), Shangyao (Upper Yaos), Xiayao (Lower Yaos), and Juyao (Position Yaos) are crucial for addressing lower back pain. The Zhimen (Will Gate) and Jingmen (Capital Gate) are also critical for lower back pain and spinal discomfort.[113p]

　　小肠俞、中(月吕)俞、白环俞，主腰脊疝痛。　　次髎、胞肓、承筋，主腰脊痛恶寒。　　三里、阴市、阳辅、蠡沟，主腰痛不可以顾。　　束骨、飞扬、承筋，主腰痛如折。
　　申脉、太冲、阳蹺，主腰痛不能举。　　昆仑，主脊强背尻骨重。
　　合阳，主腰脊痛引腹。
　　委中，主腰痛挟脊至头，八八然。凡腰脚重痛，于此刺出血，久痼宿疹，亦皆立已。　　大锺，主腰脊痛。[114p]

Xiao Changyu, Zhong (Yue) Yu, and Baihuan Yu are responsible for alleviating pain due to lumbar and spinal hernias.

Ciliao, Baohuang, and Chengjin are associated with lumbar and spinal pain with chills.

Sanli, Yin Market, Yang Auxiliary, and Ligu are for lumbar pain that prevents turning.

Shugu, Feiyang, and Chengjin are for lumbar pain that feels like it's broken.

Shenmai, Taichong, and Yangqiao are for lumbar pain that makes it impossible to lift.

Kunlun is for strengthening the spine and alleviating weight in the lower back.

Heyang is for lumbar and spinal pain that radiates to the abdomen.

Weizhong is for lumbar pain that travels up the spine to the head, often with a profound sensation. For persistent heavy pain in the lower back and legs, bloodletting at these points can provide immediate relief.

Dazhong is for lumbar and spinal pain.[114p]

　　太白、阴陵泉、行间，主腰痛不可俯仰。　　承扶，主腰脊尻臀股阴寒痛。
　　涌泉，主腰脊相引如解。
　　阴谷[阴谷　原作「阴骨」，据《千金》卷三十改。]，主脊内廉痛。　　膈关，秩边、京骨，主背恶寒痛，脊强难以俯仰。　　《儒门事亲》曰：肾俞二穴，在十四椎下两旁各寸半陷中，灸五壮，主腰痛不可俯仰，转侧难，身寒热，食倍多，身羸瘦，面黄黑，目(目巟)(目巟)；又主丈夫妇人冷疾，气劳病。中膂俞二穴，在十一椎下两旁各寸半，灸五壮，主腰痛不可俯仰，挟脊膂痛，上下按之应手者，从项后始至此穴，痛皆灸之，立愈也。　　腰俞一穴，在二十一椎节下间陷中，灸五壮，主腰疼不能久立，腰以下至足冷不仁，起坐难，腰脊痛不能立，急强不得俯，腰重如石，难举动也。　　张仲文传神仙灸法：腰膝重痛不可转侧，起坐难，及冷痹，脚筋挛急，不可转侧屈伸，灸曲膝两文头左右脚四处各三壮。[115p]

Tai Bai, Yin Ling Quan, and Xing Jian are points that indicate lower back pain that makes it difficult to bend or stretch.

Cheng Fu indicates pain in the lower back, spine, buttocks, and thighs due to cold.

Yong Quan indicates a pulling sensation in the lower back and spine, as if being relieved.

Yin Gu, originally written as "Yin Gu," which has been corrected to "Yin Gu" according to the "Qian Jin," indicates pain in the inner spine.

Ge Guan, Zhi Bian, and Jing Gu, indicate severe cold pain in the back and a stiff spine, making it hard to bend or stretch.

The "Ru Men Shi Qin" states: The Shen Yu points, two located an inch and a half on either side below the 14th vertebra, if moxibusted five times, indicate lower back pain that makes it difficult to bend or stretch, difficulty in turning, alternating cold and heat in the body, excessive appetite, thinness, a pale or dark complexion, with eyes (the last part is unclear); they also indicate cold diseases in men and women, and fatigue-related ailments.

The Zhong Liu Yu points, two located an inch and a half on either side below the 11th vertebra, if moxibusted five times, indicate lower back pain that makes it difficult to bend or stretch, with pain alongside the spine. Pressing up and down from the neck to this point should elicit pain, and all painful areas should be treated with moxibustion for immediate relief.

The Yao Yu point is located in the depression below the 21st vertebra; moxibustion five times here helps with lower back pain that prevents one from standing for long, causing coldness and numbness from the waist down to the feet, making it hard to rise or sit, with a heavy sensation in the lower back like stone that makes movement difficult.

Zhang Zhongwen described a method for treating spirit immortals: with heavy pain in the lower back and knees making it hard to turn, rise, or sit, as well as cold blockages, and tightness in the leg tendons that restrict movement, moxibustion should be applied to both knees at the two points on the top, three times each on both feet in various locations.[115p]

每灸一脚二火齐下，艾炷到肉，初觉疼痛，用二人两边齐吹至火灭。午时着灸，人定已来，脏腑自动一两行，或转动如雷声，其疾立愈。此法神效，卒不可量也。　　朱震亨《心法》曰：腰曲不能伸者，针人中。　　《医学纲目》曰：《素问》刺腰痛篇，刺足太阳腰痛引项脊尻背，三法刺郄中出血，二法取足太阳出血也。　　经云：邪在肾，腹胀腰痛，大便难，肩背颈项痛，时眩，取之涌泉、昆仑，视有血者悉取之。此则足太阳、少阴俱取血也。又云：足太阳之脉，是动则病冲头痛云云；此则视太阳盛虚热寒陷下，刺施补泻疾留，灸以调之也。　　刺足少阴腰痛，引脊内廉，此法出足少阴经血也。经曰：足少阴之别，名曰大锺，当踝后，绕踝别走太阳，其病虚则腰痛，取之所别也，此补足少阴络也。　　刺腰痛不可俯仰四法，少阳、阳明衡络三法，皆出血也。[116p]

For every moxibustion, two fires are applied simultaneously. The moxa reaches the flesh, and initially, one feels pain. Two people then blow on either side until the fire is extinguished. When applied at noon, the individual has already settled; the internal organs react spontaneously, sometimes moving as if accompanied by thunder, leading to immediate recovery. This method is extraordinarily effective and cannot be quantified.

Zhu Zhenheng in "Heart Techniques" states: If the waist is bent and cannot be straightened, needle the Ren (Conception) point.

The "Medical Guidelines" states: According to the "Plain Questions," for lumbar pain, needling the foot's Taiyang point relieves pain radiating to the neck, spine, and lower back. The three methods involve needling the valley to draw blood, two methods involve drawing blood from the foot's Taiyang point as well.

The Classic states: If the pathogen is in the kidneys, symptoms include abdominal distention, lumbar pain, difficulty with bowel movements, and pain in the shoulders, back, and neck, often accompanied by dizziness; treat the Yongquan (Gushing Spring) and Kunlun (Kunlun Mountains) points, and withdraw blood as necessary. This treatment draws blood from both the foot's Taiyang and Shaoyin channels.

Additionally, it is stated that the channel of the foot's Taiyang, when disturbed, can cause dizziness and headaches; hence, one should observe the balance of Taiyang, whether it is strong or deficient in heat or cold, to determine needling techniques for immediate adjustment.

For lumbar pain in the foot’s Shaoyin channel, needle along the inner side of the spine to draw blood from the foot's Shaoyin channel. The Classic notes that the branch of the foot's Shaoyin is called the "Great Bell," located behind the ankle, circling near to the Taiyang. If there is deficiency, lumbar pain results, so treating the branch is necessary to nourish the foot's Shaoyin network.

For lumbar pain, needling shouldn't be done while bending or looking upwards; three methods from the Shaoyang and Yangming channels all involve bloodletting.[116p]

经云：肝足厥阴之脉，是动则病腰痛不可以俯仰，此则视虚实寒热陷下，施补泻疾留，灸以调之也。　　刺腰痛引少腹控(月少)，不可以仰，取腰尻分间，经文三出，此其一也。缪刺论云：腰痛引少腹控(月少)，不可以仰息，刺腰尻之解，两胂之上，是腰俞，以月死生为痏数，发针立已，左刺右，右刺左。又骨空论云：腰痛不可以转摇，急引阴卵，刺八髎与痛上，八髎在腰尻分间。此三节经文大同小异，通一法也。又足厥阴之脉，是动则病腰痛，不可以俯仰，视盛虚热寒陷下调之，此则证同法异。　　刺腰痛目(目巟)(目巟)有三：昌阳之脉其一也；若痛引肩遗溲者，刺解脉，在郄外廉筋肉分间，委阳穴也；若痛引项脊欲僵仆者，刺足太阳委中出血也。　　刺腰痛篇取足太阳郄腘中间六法。郄腘者，膝后屈处两筋之间，横文腘内也。[117p]

The classic text states: The liver foot jueyin meridian, when it moves, causes pain in the lower back, making it impossible to bend or look up. This should be treated by assessing the conditions of deficiency or excess, cold or heat, and applying tonification or sedation techniques, along with moxibustion for regulation. To treat pain in the lower back radiating to the lower abdomen (the lesser moon), one cannot look up; the needling is applied at the waist-hindquarters junction, with three references in the classic texts, of which this is one. The Treatise on Acupuncture states: Pain in the lower back radiating to the lower abdomen (the lesser moon) makes it impossible to lie back. Needling the solution at the waist-hindquarters, above the two tendons, is known as the lumbar shu point, using the cyclical rhythm of the moon to guide the treatment, alternating needling left and right. Furthermore, the Treatise on Bone Cavities states: Pain in the lower back prevents turning or shaking, quickly affecting the lower yin; needling the eight sacral points along with the area of pain, located at the waist-hindquarters junction. These three sections of classic texts have largely similar meanings and share a unified method. Additionally, the liver foot jueyin meridian, upon movement, causes lower back pain, making it impossible to bend or look up. The conditions of excess or deficiency and heat or cold can be assessed for treatment; hence while the symptoms are the same, the treatment methods differ.

For treating lower back pain, there are three main approaches: one is related to the yangming channel; if pain radiates to the shoulder with urinary issues, needling the solution point is done at the muscular and tendon junction outside the xie; if pain radiates to the nape and spine with stiffness or risk of collapsing, needling the foot taiyang at the yong point is indicated. For lower back pain, the section discusses six methods at the foot taiyang channel point in the middle of the popliteal area. The popliteal area is at the back of the knee, situated between the two tendons, horizontally within the popliteal cavity.[117p]

太阴正经二法，刺郄中央出血。解脉二法，刺郄中横文出血。衡络一法，刺郄上数寸出血。会阴一法，刺郄中下五寸出血也。　　肾虚腰痛，刺肾腧，取法以杖量与脐平，去脊各一寸半，灸二七壮。又取人中、委中。　　腰强痛，灸命门二七壮，十四椎节下间，伏取之，刺昆仑泻之，灸亦泻。　　忽然气滞腰痛，不可俯仰，取志室五分，得气即泻，又取行间。　　腰脊内引痛，不可屈伸，若近上痛取合谷，近下痛取昆仑、复溜。　　腰脊俱痛不可忍，取风池、合谷、昆仑。　　又法，风池、承山、合谷、吕细、三间。　　腰脊如痓，取涌泉一分，阴谷一寸半，京骨一分，行间五分。　　腰闪挫气痛，取尺泽，忌灸。又取委中、人中、阳陵泉、束骨、昆仑、下髎。　　肾虚痛久不已，取肩井、肾俞五分，留七呼，灸随年壮。　　腰痛刺之不定者，刺八髎。[118p]

The two methods of the Taiyin channel involve needling the central point of the Hui to induce bleeding. The two methods of resolving the pulse involve needling the horizontal line through the Hui to induce bleeding. One method to balance the collaterals involves needling a few inches above the Hui to induce bleeding. One method at the Hui involves needling five inches below to induce bleeding.

For kidney deficiency causing lower back pain, needle the kidney point, measuring with a stick level with the navel, one and a half inches away from the spine on each side, and moxibustion for twenty-seven times. Also needle the Renzhong and Weizhong points.

For tight lower back pain, moxibustion at Mingmen for twenty-seven times, targeting the space between the fourteenth vertebrae, press down to take it, needle Kunlun for sedation, and use moxibustion for sedation as well.

For sudden energy stagnation resulting in back pain that prevents bending or stretching, needle Zhi Shi five fen, and once obtaining qi, sedate it; also needle the Xing Jian point.

For internal pulling pain in the lumbar spine that prevents bending or extending, if the pain is higher, take He Gu, and if lower, take Kun Lun and Fu Liu.

For unbearable pain in both the lumbar and spinal areas, needle Feng Chi, He Gu, and Kun Lun.

Another method includes Feng Chi, Cheng Shan, He Gu, Lu Xi, and San Jian.

For sensations resembling spasm in the lumbar spine, needle Yong Quan by one fen, Yin Gu by one and a half inches, Jing Gu by one fen, and Xing Jian by five fen.

For back pain from twisting or impacting, needle Chi Ze and avoid moxibustion. Also needle Weizhong, Renzhong, Yang Ling Quan, Shu Gu, Kun Lun, and Xia Liao.

For chronic kidney deficiency pain that does not resolve, needle Jian Jing and Shen Xu by five fen, retaining the needle for seven breaths, and apply moxibustion according to the course of the year.

For lower back pain where needling does not stabilize, needle Ba Liao.[118p]

　　大虚腰痛，刺而复发，腰重不能举体，可刺委中动脉出血。　　腰痛在身之前，取足阳明原穴；身之后，取足太阳原穴；身之侧，取足少阳原穴。　　闪着腰痛，取气海，肥人一寸，瘦人五分，三补三泻，令人觉脐上下痛停针。候二十五息，左手重按其穴，右手进针，三息；又停二十五息，依前进针，令人觉从外肾热气上入小腹，出针，神效。　　《古今医统》曰：腰痛宜用雷火针法，于五月五日，东引桃枝削去皮尖两头，如鸡子样，长寸许用尖，针时以针向灯上点着，用纸三层或五层，贴在患处，以针按纸上，患深者再燃立愈。呪曰：天火地火，三昧真火，针天天开，针地地裂，针鬼鬼灭。针人人得长生，百病消除，万病消灭。吾奉太上老君急急如律令。　　《医学入门》曰：腰痛，轻者委中出血便愈；甚者补环跳、泻委中；久者俱补。　　腰连背痛者，针昆仑、委中。[119p]

Severe lower back pain, which recurs after acupuncture, leads to a sensation of heaviness in the lower back making it difficult to lift the body. One can puncture the Weizhong point to stop bleeding.

For lower back pain felt at the front of the body, use the foot Yangming source point; at the back, use the foot Taiyang source point; to the side of the body, use the foot Shaoyang source point.

For acute lower back pain, needle the Qihai point; for overweight individuals, insert the needle one inch deep, and for those who are thin, five-tenths. Alternate between reinforcement and draining techniques to relieve the pain, making the patient feel the pain in the upper and lower abdomen before removing the needle. After a pause of twenty-five breaths, press firmly on the point with the left hand while inserting the needle with the right for three breaths; pause again for twenty-five breaths and repeat, making the patient feel the warm energy from the external kidneys rising into the lower abdomen; then remove the needle for effective relief.

The "Ancient and Modern Medical Compilation" states: for lower back pain, one should use the method of lightning fire needles. On the fifth day of the fifth month, take a peach branch, trim both ends like an egg, and use it as a needle about an inch long. Ignite the needle at a flame, and, using three or five layers of paper, apply it to the affected area, pressing the needle onto the paper. For deep-seated issues, reignite the needle for immediate improvement. Recite: "Heavenly fire, earthly fire, true fire of Samadhi; with the needle, heaven opens, the earth splits, and the needle extinguishes spirits. Those who receive this needle attain longevity, all ailments are eliminated, and countless diseases are eradicated. I follow the command of the Supreme Laojun urgently as per the law."

The "Introduction to Medicine" states: for lower back pain, mild cases can be treated by bleeding from Weizhong; for severe cases, tonify Huantiao and drain Weizhong; for chronic pain, both points should be tonified.

For lower back pain that radiates to the back, needle the Kunlun and Weizhong points.[119p]

　　腰连腿痛，补腕骨，泻足三里。
　　腰连脚痛，补环跳，泻风市、行间、足三里。　　命门，主老人肾虚腰痛。

　　　　导引

　　《千金方》曰：腰痛导引法，正东坐，收手抱心，一人于前据摄其两膝，一人后捧其头，徐牵令偃卧，头到地，三起三卧，久久效。　　《保生秘要》曰：气血虚弱，濇于肾，诸寒收引，皆属肾水气弱，或作腰痛。冬月水旺，宜吐纳按节，吹气调和，会意掌心。所忌须避寒冷，最宜早卧。大抵冬月敛藏气闭，至阴已极，宜节欲，养一阳之初生。盖阴阳交精子南合璧，万物气微在下，不可动摇，守此，则保寿无疆。　　腰痛导引法：相火烧两肾，或以手心摩热，以擦痛处。　　腰风软导引法：肾处相火提起烧背，从背转下于肾。[120p]

Lower back pain connected to the legs, supplement with wrist bones, and drain the point Zusanli.
Lower back pain connected to the feet, supplement with Huantiao, and drain Fengshi, Xingjian, and Zusanli. The Mingmen point is associated with elderly kidney deficiency leading to back pain.

Guidance

The "Thousand Gold Prescriptions" states: For back pain guidance, sit facing east, collect the hands to embrace the heart. One person holds both knees in the front, and another supports the head from behind. Gradually pull to lie down, with the head touching the ground, rise and lie down three times, repeat this for a long time to be effective. The "Essentials for Preserving Life" states: When qi and blood are weak, it is related to the kidneys; various cold factors draw in, all belong to weakness of kidney water qi, which may lead to back pain. In winter, when water is abundant, it is advisable to practice breathing techniques and regulate the flow of air. Avoid cold and favor going to bed early. Generally, in winter, the energy is retracted and closed, reaching extreme cold; one should regulate desires to nourish the initial growth of yang. For yin and yang to unite, the essence must harmonize; all things are subtly grounded and should not be shaken. If you maintain this, you will preserve your longevity without bounds. Back pain guidance: let the fire of the kidney bring warmth, or rub the heated palms on the painful area. For lumbar wind soft guidance: raise the fire in the kidneys to warm the back, then transfer this heat down to the kidneys.[120p]

　　　　　医案

　　《史记》仓公传曰：齐王黄姬兄黄长卿家有酒召客，召臣意。诸客坐未上食，臣意望见王后弟宋建，告曰：君有病往四五日，君腰胁痛，不可俯仰，又不得小溲，不亟治，病即入濡肾，及其未舍五脏，急治之。病方今客肾濡，此所谓肾痹也。宋建曰：然。建故有腰脊痛往四五日，天雨，黄氏诸倩，见建家京下方石即弄之，建亦欲效之，效之不能起，即复置之。暮腰脊痛，不得溺，至今不愈。建病得之好持重。所以知建病者，臣意见其色太阳色干，肾部上及界腰以下者，枯四分所，故以往四五日知其发也。臣意即为柔汤使服之，十八日所而病愈。
　　济北王侍者韩女病腰背痛寒热，众医皆以为寒热也。臣意诊脉曰：内寒，月事不下也。即窜以药，旋下，病已。病得之欲男子而不可得也。所以知韩女之病者，诊其脉时，切之肾脉也，濇而不属，其来难坚，故曰月事不下。肝脉弦出左寸口，故曰欲男子不可得也。[121p]

Medical Case

The "Records of the Historian" in the biography of Cang Gong states: The brother of King Huang Ji of Qi, Huang Changqing, hosted a banquet for guests, as was the custom. While the guests were seated but had not yet begun to eat, I noticed the younger brother of the queen, Song Jian, and informed him: "You have been ill for four to five days, experiencing pain in your lower back and flanks. You cannot bend or stretch, nor can you urinate. If not treated urgently, this condition will affect your kidneys, compromising your five vital organs. Immediate care is essential. The illness you currently have is an obstruction in the kidneys, which is known as kidney wind." Song Jian acknowledged this. He had indeed suffered from back pain for four to five days; due to the rainy weather, the people of the Huang family were playing with stones near his house, and he too desired to emulate them, but he was unable to rise after attempting. By evening, his back pain worsened, and he could not urinate; he remains unwell to this day.

For his condition, I conclude that he must maintain a careful demeanor. Therefore, I observed his symptoms and noted that his complexion had a dry, sunken hue, and that the area above his kidneys and below his waist appeared withered. This indicates that I recognized his onset four to five days earlier. I prescribed a gentle decoction for him, and after eighteen days, he recovered.

Regarding the case of the maidservant of the King of Jibei, Han, who suffered from back pain coupled with cold and heat symptoms, many doctors diagnosed it as a cold-heat condition. However, upon feeling her pulse, I observed internal cold, which correlates with her menstruation being absent. I adjusted her medication swiftly, and her condition improved immediately. The reason for her illness was a desire for a male child that was unfulfilled. Therefore, while diagnosing Han’s illness, I noted that when feeling her pulse, I checked her kidney pulse, which was weak and not connected, indicating difficulty with her condition, hence her menstruation was not coming. The liver pulse, detected at the left inch, indicated her desire for a male child that could not be obtained.[121p]

　　《儒门事亲》曰：戴人女僮冬间自途来，面赤如火，至(氵隐)阳病胯腰大痛，里急后重，痛则见鬼神。戴人曰：此少阳经也，在身侧为相火。使服舟车丸、通经散，泻至数盆，病犹未瘥。人皆怪之，以为有祟。戴人大怒曰：驴鬼也！复合调胃承气汤二两，加牵牛头末一两同煎服之，太过数十行，约一二缶，方舍其杖策，但发渴。戴人恣其饮水、西瓜、梨、柿等，曰：凡治火莫如冰。水，天地之至阴也。约饮水一二桶，犹觉微痛。戴人乃刺其阳陵穴以伸其滞，足少阳胆经之穴也。自是方宁。女僮自言：每一岁须泻五六次，今年不曾泻，故如是也。常仲明悟其言，以身有湿病，故一岁必泻十余行，病始已。此可与智者言，难与愚者论也。[122p]

The "Rituals of the Confucian School" states: A servant girl of Dai, while traveling in winter, arrived with her face red as fire. Upon reaching (Shuiyin), she suffered severe pain in her waist and experienced urgency with a heavy sensation in her lower abdomen, and when the pain occurred, she claimed to see spirits. Dai, the physician, said: This pertains to the Shaoyang channel; the fire is located at the side of the body. He prescribed medicinal pills and decoction to harmonize the channels, and after several purgative treatments, the illness had not yet healed. People were puzzled and thought she was possessed. Dai, in anger, exclaimed: It’s a donkey spirit! He then adjusted the gastrointestinal harmonizing decoction and combined it with one measure of the powdered root of the Qian Niu Tou, cooking and administering it. The treatment induced a plentiful cramping, about one or two bowls in total, and then she cast aside her cane, only feeling thirst. Dai allowed her to drink as much water as she wanted, along with watermelon, pears, and persimmons, saying: In treating fire, nothing compares to ice. Water is the ultimate form of yin from heaven and earth. After drinking one or two buckets, she still felt slight pain. Dai then needled her Yanglingquan point to relieve the stagnation, which is the point on the foot corresponding to the Shaoyang gallbladder channel. From this treatment onward, she felt at ease. The maidservant then mentioned: Every year, I must purge five or six times; this year I haven't purged, which is why I feel this way.常仲, understanding her words keenly, realized that due to her damp illness, he also must purge more than ten times a year, thus the onset of his ailment. This can be discussed with the wise, but is difficult to explain to the foolish.[122p]

　　息师病腰股沉痛，行步坐马皆不便。或作脚气寒湿治之，或作虚损治之，乌、附、乳、没活血壮筋骨之药，无不用之，至六十余日，目赤上热，大小便濇，腰股之病如故。戴人诊其两手脉皆沉迟，沉者为在里也，在里者泻之，以舟车丸、浚川散各一服，去积水二十余行，至早辰服虀白粥一二顿，与之马，已能矍烁矣。[123p]

The patient suffers from a painful lower back and hips, making it difficult to walk or ride. Some treat it as a case of cold dampness affecting the feet, while others see it as a deficiency. Various invigorating and blood-stimulating medicines, including black, aconite, motherwort, and myrrh, were used extensively. After over sixty days, the symptoms persisted: red eyes, internal heat, and troubled urination, while the back and hips remained the same. A physician examined the patient's pulse and found both wrists to be deep and slow, indicating an internal issue that required purging. Administered were doses of Zhou Che Wan and Jun Chuan San, eliminating over twenty blocks of stagnant water. After a morning meal of thin rice porridge and some horse, the patient regained significant vitality.[123p]

　　一男子六十余岁，病腰尻脊胯皆痛，数载不愈，昼静夜躁，大痛往来，屡求自尽天年。且夕则痛作，必令人以手槌击，至五更鸡鸣则渐减，向曙则痛止。左右及病者，皆作鬼神阴谴白虎嚙，朝祷暮祝，觋巫、僧道、禁师至，则其痛以减。又梦鬼神战鬬相击，山川神庙无不祭者。淹延岁月，肉瘦皮枯，饮食减少，暴怒日增，惟候一死。有书生曰：既云鬼神虎嚙阴谴之祸，如此祷祈，何无一应？闻陈郡有张戴人精于医，可以问其鬼神白虎与病乎？彼若术穷，可以委命。其家从之。戴人诊其两手脉皆沉滞坚劲，力如张絙，谓之曰：病虽瘦，难于食，然腰尻脊胯皆痛者，必大便坚燥。[124p]

A man over sixty years old suffered from pain in his lower back, hips, and spine, which had persisted for several years without relief. He experienced quiet during the day but restless nights, with severe pain coming and going, leading him to repeatedly seek to end his life. His pain intensified in the evening, requiring others to strike him with a pestle, but it would gradually reduce by the time the rooster crowed at dawn, and cease by morning. Those around him, as well as the patient himself, believed that spirits and supernatural beings were punishing him with the bite of a white tiger. They prayed fervently day and night, causing shamans, monks, and practitioners of various religious disciplines to come, which seemed to alleviate his pain. He also dreamed of battles among spirits, and offered sacrifices to every mountain, river, and shrine without exception. As time passed, he became emaciated and dehydrated, his appetite diminished, and his anger grew, as he awaited death.

A scholar suggested that since the trouble stemmed from the spirits and the biting of the tiger, despite their prayers, there had been no response. He heard of a man named Zhang Dai from Chen County, skilled in medicine, and suggested consulting him about his affliction from the white tiger and the spirits. If he lacked a solution, he could entrust his fate. The man’s family followed this advice. Zhang Dai examined his pulse, which was heavy, stagnant, and rigid, with a strength similar to that of a stretched bow. He informed them: despite the man's emaciation and difficulty in eating, the pain in his lower back, hips, and spine indicated that his bowel movements were likely hard and dry.[124p]

其左右曰：有五七日或八九日，见燥粪一两块如弹丸，结硬不可言，曾令人剜取之，强下一两块，浑身燥痒，皮肤皴揭，枯濇如麸片。戴人既得病之虚实，随用大承气汤以姜枣煎之，加牵牛头末二钱，不敢言是泻剂。盖病者闻暖则悦，闻寒则惧，说补则从，说泻则逆，此弊非一日也，而况一齐人傅之，众楚人咻之乎？及煎成，使稍热咽之，从少至多，累至三日，天且晚，脏腑下泄四五行，约半盆，以灯视之，皆燥粪痞块及瘀血，秽浊不可近，须臾痛减九分，昏睡鼻息调如常人。睡至明日将夕，始觉饥而索粥，温凉与之。又困睡一二日，其痛全愈。次令饮食调养，日服导水丸、甘露散，滑利便溺之药，四十余日乃复。病既痊，乃寿至八十岁。故凡燥证，皆三阳病也。[125p]

His attendants said: "After five to seven days, or even eight to nine days, we saw small hard lumps of dry feces, like pellets, which were so hardened that they could not be described. We had someone fetch them, and after forcibly taking out one or two lumps, the patient experienced dryness and itching all over, with the skin peeling and becoming as dehydrated as dried dough. Once we understood the patient's condition, we used a major purgative decoction boiled with ginger and jujube and added two qian of the powdered root of the qian niu tou (milk vetch). We dared not call it a purgative. It was because the patient found warmth pleasurable and feared the cold; when we said it would be nourishing, he accepted it, but when we mentioned purging, he resisted. Such a condition does not develop overnight, especially when surrounded by those who supported him, and the people of Chu encouraged him. After boiling the mixture, we allowed him to swallow it slightly warm, starting with small amounts and gradually increasing over three days. By the evening of that third day, the organs had expelled four to five liters, about half a basin. Upon inspection by lantern light, the liquid consisted entirely of dry feces, hard masses, and stagnant blood—filthy and unapproachable. In a short while, the pain reduced by nine-tenths, and he fell into a deep sleep, breathing regularly like a normal person. By the next day towards evening, he felt hungry and asked for porridge, which we gave him warm. After one or two more days of rest, all his pain had entirely healed. Next, we advised him to adjust his diet for nourishment and to take the dao shui wan (water guiding pills) and gan lu san (sweet dew powder), medicines that promoted smooth urination and defecation. It took more than forty days for him to fully recover. Once the illness was cured, he lived to be eighty years old. Therefore, all dry conditions are considered illnesses of the three yang."[125p]

　　北人卫德新因之析津，冬月饮寒则冷，病腰常直，不能屈伸，两足沉重，难于行步，途中以床畀递程。问医，皆云肾虚，以苁蓉、巴戟、附子、鹿茸皆用之，大便反闭，潮热上周，将经岁矣，乃乞拯于戴人。戴人曰：此疾十日之效耳。卫曰：一月亦非迟。戴人曰：足太阳经血多，病则腰似折，腘如结，腨如裂。太阳所至，为屈伸不利。况腰者肾之府也，身中之大关节，今既强直而不利，宜咸以软之，顿服则和柔矣。《难经》曰：强力入房，则肾伤而髓枯，枯则高骨乃坏而不用，与此正同。今君之证，太阳为寒所遏，血坠下滞腰间，必有积血，非肾虚也。节次以药下数百行，约去血一二(豆斗)，次以九曲玲珑灶蒸之，汗出三五次而愈。初蒸时至五日，问曰：腹中鸣否？德新曰：未也。至六日觉鸣，七日而起，已能揖人。戴人曰：病有热者勿蒸，蒸则损人目也。[126p]

The northern man, Wei Dexin, encountered a diagnosis of illness at Xijiang during the winter months, suffering from coldness and persistent back pain, unable to bend or stretch. His legs felt heavy, making it difficult to walk, so he was carried on a bed along the way. Upon consulting doctors, they all stated it was due to kidney deficiency, recommending the use of herbs like cistanche, bark of the Baijiguo, aconite, and deer antler. However, he experienced constipation and tidal fever for almost a year, so he sought help from Doctor Dai. Doctor Dai remarked that this illness would show improvement in ten days, to which Wei replied that a month would not be too late.

Doctor Dai explained that when the kidney's energy in the foot yang meridian is excessive, it can lead to back pain as if it were broken, causing stiffness in the knees and discomfort in the lower back. The cold from the yang meridian obstructed the body, making bending and stretching difficult. Moreover, the lower back is the house of the kidneys and a vital joint in the body. Given its rigidity and hindrance, it should be softened. When taken suddenly, the body would become harmonious and flexible.

The Nan Jing states: If one engages in strong physical activity, the kidneys can be harmed, and marrow may dry up, leading to damage to the bones, which is similar to this case. In Wei's condition, the yang meridian was obstructed by cold, causing stagnation of blood in the lower back. This was not merely kidney deficiency.

Following a regimen with medication over several hundred dosages, roughly one or two bean measures of blood were drawn. After that, he was treated with steaming from a special stove, resulting in sweating three to five times which led to recovery. Initially, after five days of steaming, Doctor Dai inquired if there was any sound from the stomach. Wei replied no, but by the sixth day, he felt it gurgling, and by the seventh day, he was able to greet others respectfully. Doctor Dai cautioned that those with heat should avoid steaming, as it could harm the eyes.[126p]

　　息城酒监赵进道病腰痛，岁余不愈，其两手脉沉实有力。以通经散下五七行，次以杜仲去粗皮细切炒断丝为细末，每服三钱，猪腰子一枚薄批五七片，先以椒盐腌去腥水，掺药在内，裹以荷叶，外以湿纸数重，以文武火烧熟，临卧细嚼，以温酒送下，每旦以无比山药丸一服，数日而愈。
　　《东垣十书》曰：末年冬，曹通甫自河南来，有役人小翟露宿寒湿之地，腰痛不能转侧，两胁搐急作痛，已经月余不愈矣。腰痛论中说皆为足大阳、足少阴血络中有凝血作痛，间有一二证属少阳胆经外络脉病，皆去血络之凝乃愈。其《内经》有云：冬三月禁不得用针，只宜服药，通其经络，破其血络中败血。[127p]

Zhao Jin, the wine supervisor of Xicheng, suffered from chronic lower back pain for over a year without improvement. His pulse was deep, strong, and solid. He used a formula containing Tong Jing San and took five to seven doses. Next, he prepared a fine powder of prepared Eucommia Bark, cutting it finely after removing the coarse skin, and took three qian (a measurement) each time. He took one pig kidney, sliced it thinly into five to seven pieces, and marinated it with pepper and salt to remove the fishy smell. He mixed the medicine inside, wrapped it in lotus leaves, and securely covered it with wet paper numerous times, then cooked it with both gentle and intense fire until done. He chewed it finely before lying down, washing it down with warm wine. Every morning, he took a dose of Wubi Shanyao Wan, and after a few days, he was cured.

The "Ten Books of Dongyuan" states: In the last year of winter, Cao Tongfu came from Henan and found a laborer named Xiao Zhai who had to sleep in a cold and damp place. He suffered from back pain and was unable to turn over, with acute pain in both sides. He had already been suffering for more than a month without improvement. The discussions on back pain indicate that this is due to coagulated blood in the blood vessels of the foot's yangming and shaoyin, with one or two cases belonging to the shaoyang gallbladder channel. Only by resolving the blood coagulation could he be cured. The "Inner Canon" states: In the winter months, one should avoid using needles and should only take medicine to unblock the meridians and break the stagnant blood within the vessels.[127p]

　　《丹溪心法》曰：徐质夫年六十，因坠马腰痛，不可转侧，六脉散大，重取则弦小而长稍坚。予以为恶血虽有，未可驱逐，且以补接为先，遂令煎苏木、人参、黄芪、川芎、当归、陈皮、甘草，服至半月后，散大渐敛，饮食亦进。遂与前药，调下自然铜等药，服一月而安。
　　义一侄妇疟疾初安，因冲风又发腰痛白浊，已与参、朮、槟榔、半夏等补方，又教以煅牡蛎一钱，木通五分，炒蘗三分，粗末，入前方同煎而愈。
　　《医学纲目》曰：戊戌年八月，淮南大水，城下浸灌者连月，予忽脏腑不调，腹中如水吼，数日调治得愈。自此腰痛不可屈折，虽洗面亦相妨，遍服药不效，如是凡三月。予后思之，此必水气阴盛，肾经感此而得，乃灸肾俞三七壮，服麋茸丸瘥。[128p]

The "Danxi Heart Method" states: Xu Zhifu, sixty years old, fell off a horse and suffered from back pain, making it impossible to turn. His six pulses were scattered and large, but when re-examined, they were thin and slightly firm. I believed that although there was stasis of evil blood, it should not be forcibly expelled, and first needed to replenish and reconnect. Therefore, I prescribed a decoction of sandalwood, ginseng, astragalus, chuanxiong, angelica, tangerine peel, and licorice, which he took for half a month. Gradually, the scattered pulses became more stable, and his appetite improved. I then combined these herbs with natural copper and others, and after a month, he was well.

Yiyi's niece, who initially recovered from intermittent fever, suffered from back pain and turbid discharge due to being exposed to wind. She had already been given a tonic with ginseng, poria, betel nut, and pinellia, and I instructed her to take one qian of calcined oyster, five fen of houttuynia, and three fen of fried woad, ground coarse, and to combine these with the previous prescription. She recovered.

The "Medical Compendium" states: In the eighth month of the Wuxu year, there were severe floods in Huainan, and the city was submerged for months. I suddenly felt an imbalance in my organs, with a roaring sensation in my abdomen like water. After several days of treatment, I recovered. Since then, I have experienced persistent back pain, making it difficult to bend, and even washing my face was troublesome. I took all kinds of medications without effect for three months. I later realized that this must have been due to an excess of water and cold dampness affecting the kidney meridian. I then performed moxibustion on the kidney shu point three times, and took deer antler pills, which led to my recovery.[128p]

　　《医学准绳六要》曰：一人因太劳，又过饮酒，致湿热乘虚入客于经，作腰痛，夜更甚，不得俯仰，脉濡而弱。先与拈痛汤去参、朮二贴稍愈，遂改用四物加杜仲、牛膝、独活、肉桂顿愈。
　　一人肥盛而肢节痛，腰更甚，脉沉濡而滑，知湿痰也，予二陈加南星、二朮、二活、秦艽、防风十剂愈。
　　一人体厚，腰间常冷，予肾着汤加南星、苍朮三服愈。
　　一人因堕马，腰痛不止，日轻夜重，瘀血谛矣，与四物去地黄，加肉桂、桃仁、红花、苏木四服，大便下血而痊。
　　一人素有脚气，每发则引腰痛，不可俯仰。其人雄饮，明是湿热，脉濡而数，投拈痛汤八剂渐减，遂以捉虎丹酒下二丸，空心凡三服，腿腕出黑汗，永不再举。
　　《奇效良方》曰：忠州太守陈逢原因暑取凉食瓜，至秋忽然右腰腿间疼痛，连及膝胫，曲折不能，经月右脚难于举动。凡治腰脚药，服之无效，得养肾散才一服，移刻举身淋痹，再服脚能屈伸，再一服即康宁。[129p]

"The Essentials of Medical Principles" states: A person who was overly fatigued and excessively drank alcohol developed damp-heat that invaded the channels, resulting in waist pain, which worsened at night, making it impossible to bend or look up, with a pulse that was slippery and weak. Initially treated with the Pain Relief Decoction, removing ginseng and atractylodes, showed slight improvement, so the prescription was changed to Four Substance Decoction with additional Eucommia, Achyranthes, Angelica, and Cinnamon, leading to complete recovery.

Another person, stout and experiencing pain in their joints, especially their waist, had a pulse that was deep, slippery, indicating damp phlegm. I prescribed the Two Chen Decoction with Nanshin, Atractylodes, and Qinghao, and after ten doses, recovery was achieved.

One person presented as overweight, frequently feeling cold in the waist. I administered Kidney Nourishing Decoction with Nanshin and Atractylodes for three doses, resulting in recovery.

A different individual suffered persistent waist pain after falling from a horse, with the pain worsening at night. The presence of stasis blood was confirmed; I prescribed the Four Substance Decoction, removing Rehmannia, and added Cinnamon, Peach Kernel, Safflower, and Woodsophora for four doses. Subsequently, blood was expelled from the stool, leading to healing.

Yet another person had a history of athlete's foot, where each flare-up would evoke waist pain, making movement difficult. This individual enjoyed drinking heavily, clearly indicating damp-heat, with a pulse that was slippery and rapid. After eight doses of the Pain Relief Decoction showed gradual improvement, I provided the Tiger Grasp Pill in wine, taking two pills on an empty stomach across three days. This resulted in black sweat from the legs and ankles, with no recurrence.

"The Miraculous Effective Formulas" notes: The Prefect of Zhongzhou, Chen Feng, consumed cool foods due to summer heat and suddenly in autumn experienced pain in the right waist and leg, extending to the knee, which severely limited movement for a month. Various medications aimed at treating the waist and legs were ineffective until he took the Kidney Nourishing Powder, which showed immediate results. After one dose, he could move his entire body. After another dose, he could flex and extend his legs, and one more dose led to complete health restoration.[129p]

　　一人忽两足拳挛，连腰疼楚，脉弦而濇。此证风寒两感，寒多于风，或投《百一选方》养肾散随效。李奉议亦尝谓余曰：其家曾有妇人腰脚不能转动，用此药即效。皆风寒两感之证也。
　　《薛己医案》曰：一男子年四十余，患腰痛，服流气饮、寄生汤不应，以热手熨之少可。盖脉沉弦肾虚所致，以补肾丸愈之。
　　傅允承母年踰七十，腰生一(疒畾)，作痒异常，疑虫虱所毒，诊脉浮数。齐氏云：浮数之脉而反恶寒，疮疽之谓也。又云：外如麻，里如瓜，疽毒在内。翌日复诊，脉乃弱。予谓未溃而脉先弱，何以收敛？况大便不通，则真气已竭，治之无功。其子固请，不得已，用六君子汤加霍香、神曲，饮食渐进，大便始通。更用峻补之剂，溃而脓清，作渴，再用参、芪、当归、熟地黄、麦门冬、五味子而渴止。允承喜曰：吾母可无虞矣。予谓不然，不能收敛，先人之言也。彼疑，遂速他医，果不起。[130p]

One person suddenly experienced pain in both feet and the waist, with a tight pulse and dryness. This condition indicates a simultaneous invasion of wind and cold, with cold being more pronounced. One could use the kidney-nourishing powder from the "Bai Yi Xuan Fang" with good effect. Li Fengyi also once told me that in his family, there was a woman who could not move her waist or legs, and this medicine worked immediately. This is indeed a case of simultaneous wind and cold invasion.

The "Xue Ji Medical Case" states: A man over forty suffered from lower back pain; he did not respond to the Liuqi Decoction or the Jisheng Soup. When he applied heat with his hands, it provided some relief. This was due to a deep, tight pulse indicating kidney deficiency, which was cured with kidney-replenishing pills.

Fu Yuncheng's mother, over seventy, developed a sore on her waist that caused unusual itching; it was suspected to be caused by insect bites. The pulse was floating and rapid. Qishi states that a floating and rapid pulse accompanied by chills indicates sores or abscesses. It was also said: if the surface feels like hemp and the interior feels like melon, the abscess is toxic inside. Upon re-examining the next day, the pulse was weak. I remarked that if the sore had not yet ruptured while the pulse was already weak, how could one expect to contain it? Moreover, with constipation, the vital energy was already depleted, making treatment futile. His son insisted, and with no other choice, I prescribed the Six Gentlemen Decoction with added Huo Xiang and Shen Qu, slowly advancing diet, and the bowel movement eventually began. Further, a strong tonic was used; when it ruptured, the pus was clear, and upon feeling thirsty, additional herbs—ginseng, astragalus, angelica, cooked rehmannia, ophiopogon, and schisandra—were used to stop the thirst. Yuncheng happily said, "My mother should be fine now." I disagreed, stating that it could not be contained, echoing the words of my predecessors. He was doubtful and soon sought other doctors, ultimately to no avail.[130p]

　　陆氏女初嫁，患腰痛不肿，脉沉滑神倦。此为内发七情之火，饮食之毒所致，以托里药一剂，下脓升许。陈良甫云：痈疽未溃而内陷，面青唇黑者不治。果卒。
　　昆山举人张元忠孟秋患腰疽，疮头如大豆粒，根大三寸许，微肿略赤，虚证悉具。用桑枝灸痛处，服活命饮一剂，肿退色赤，饮食仍少，用香砂六君子汤四剂，食渐进。后用大补药，脓虽成而不溃，于补药内每剂加附子一片二剂，后脓自涌出，旬日而愈。
　　一妇人暴怒，腰肿一块，胸膈不利，时或气走作痛，与方脉流气饮数剂而止，更以小柴胡汤对四物加香附、贝母，月余而愈。[131p]

A woman from the Lu family, upon her first marriage, suffered from lower back pain without swelling, her pulse was deep and slippery, and she felt fatigued. This was caused by the internal onset of the seven emotions' fire and the toxins from food. A decoction of herbal medicine was given, resulting in a discharge of pus. Chen Liangfu noted that if lesions had not yet ruptured but were inwardly festering, with a pale face and dark lips, they were untreatable. In fact, she passed away.

Zhang Yuanzhong from Kunshan, who was a scholar, suffered from a back sore in late summer; the sore was the size of a large bean, with a root about three inches long, slightly swollen and reddish, exhibiting all signs of deficiency. Moxa was applied to the painful area using mulberry branches, and he took a dose of Lifesaving Decoction, which reduced the swelling and redness, although his appetite remained poor. Then he was given a restorative herbal formula of Xiangsha Liu Junzi Tang in four doses, gradually increasing his food intake. Later, he used a highly nourishing medicine. Although pus formed, it did not rupture. He added one slice of Aconite to each dose of the nourishing medicine, and eventually, the pus flowed out on its own, leading to recovery in ten days.

A woman, suddenly enraged, developed a swelling on her lower back, with chest distress, experiencing occasional pain as qi surged. After taking several doses of Feng Mai Liu Qi Decoction, her pain ceased. She then took Xiaochaihu Decoction with modifications, adding Xiangfu and Fritillaria to the Four Substance Decoction, and after a month, she recovered.[131p]

　　一妇人腰间患一小块，肉色如常，不溃发热。予谓当以益气养荣解郁之药治之。彼家不信，别服流气饮，后针破出水，年余而殁。
　　一男子年十九，腰间肿一块，无头不痛，色不变，三月不溃，饮食少思，肌肉日瘦，此寒搏腠理，荣气不行，郁而为肿也，名曰湿毒流注。《元戎》云：若人饮食疏，精衰气血弱，肌肉消薄，荣卫之气短促而濇滞，故寒搏腠理，闭郁而为痈肿者，当补之以接虚怯之气。遂以十全大补汤加香附、陈皮三十余剂，始针之，遂出白脓二碗许，仍用前药倍加参、芪，及以豆豉饼灸之渐愈。彼惑于速效者，乃内服败毒，外贴寒凉药，反致食少脓稀，患处色紫，复请予治。喜得精神未丧，仍以前药加远志、贝母、白蔹，百剂而愈。此疮若久而不愈，或脓水清稀者，当以内塞散服之，及附子饼灸之，然后可愈。若不慎饮食起居七情者，不治。[132p]

A woman suffered a small lesion on her waist, flesh-colored as usual, without ulceration or heat. I advised that it should be treated with tonifying qi and nourishing the body, along with herbs to relieve depression. Her family did not believe this and instead took a remedy for wind. Later, it ruptured and discharged pus, and she passed away after a year.

A man, nineteen years old, had a lump on his waist that was headless and painless, with no change in color, and it did not ulcerate for three months. He had little appetite and was losing weight. This was due to cold obstructing the pores, causing the qi to stagnate and leading to swelling, which was termed damp toxin. The "Yuanrong" text states that when a person has poor appetite, weakened essence, and diminished qi and blood, with wasted muscles and obstructed protective qi, the cold blocks the pores, causing stagnation that results in abscesses and swelling. Such cases should be treated by supplementing the weak qi. Thus, I prescribed Shen Qi Wan with additional Xiang Fu and Chen Pi for over thirty doses. I then applied acupuncture, which led to the discharge of about two bowls of white pus. The previous herbs were adjusted with doubled quantities of Ren Shen and Huang Qi, and moxibustion with Dou Chi cake was used, leading to gradual recovery. However, the patient was misguided by those seeking rapid results and took a poison-expelling remedy internally and applied cooling herbs externally, which worsened his condition, leading to reduced appetite and thin pus, with the affected area turning purple. He returned for further treatment. Delighted that his spirit had not been lost, I used the previous formula, adding Yuan Zhi, Bei Mu, and Bai Lian, and after a hundred doses, he recovered. If such a sore does not heal for a long time or if the pus is clear and thin, it should be treated with an internal obstructive dispersing remedy and moxibustion with Fu Zi cake, then recovery is possible. However, if one does not carefully manage diet, daily activities, and emotions, it cannot be treated.[132p]

　　刘文通室年逾二十，腰间突肿寸许，肉色不变，微痛不溃，发热脉大。此七情所伤，气血凝滞，濇于隧道而然也。当益气血，开郁结，更以香附饼熨之，使气血充畅，内自消散，不消虽溃亦无虞。不听，乃服十宣流气之药，气血愈虚，破出清脓，不敛而毙。[133p]

Liu Wentong, over twenty years old, had a bulge about an inch wide at his waist, the color remained flesh-toned, with slight pain but no ulceration, and it felt warm with a strong pulse. This was due to emotional distress that had injured him, leading to stagnation of qi and blood, much like a blockage in a tunnel. He should tonify qi and blood, unblock the stagnation, and apply a poultice of dried ginger to promote the free flow of qi and blood, so that the internal issue could disperse; even if it did not disappear, it would pose no danger. He did not heed this advice and instead took ten prescriptions to expel qi, which only made his qi and blood even more deficient, leading to the discharge of clear pus without cessation, resulting in his death.[133p]

　　一男子腰患毒，脓熟不溃，针之脓大泄，反加烦躁，以圣愈汤四剂而宁，更以人参养荣汤，加麦门冬、五味子两月而愈。此人后患湿气，遂为痼疾。凡疮脓血去多，疮口难合，尤当补益，务使气血平复，否则更患他证，必难治疗，慎之！
　　一男子腰中患毒，发而不溃，其气血止能发起，不能培养为脓也。投大补药数剂而溃，又数剂脓尚清，乃服参芪归朮膏斤余脓少稠，数斤脓渐稠，肌肉顿生。凡大痈疽借气为主，若患而不起，或溃而不腐，或不收敛及脓少或清，皆气血之虚也，宜大补之，最忌攻伐之剂。亦有脓反多者，乃气血虚而不能禁止也。若溃后发热作渴，脉大而脓愈多，属真气虚而邪气实也，俱不治。常见气血充实之人，患疮皆肿高色赤，易腐溃而脓且稠，又易于收敛；怯弱之人多不起发不腐溃，及难于收敛。若不审察而妄投攻剂，虚脱之祸不免矣。及患后当调养，若瘰疬流注之证，尤当补益也。否则更患他证，必难措治，慎之！[134p]

A man suffered from a toxic affliction in his waist, with pus that had ripened but not broken. After being needled, the pus discharged greatly, but he became increasingly restless. Four doses of Shengyu decoction calmed him, and further doses of Ren Shen Yang Rong decoction, combined with Mai Men Dong and Wu Wei Zi over two months, brought about healing. Later, he suffered from dampness, which became a chronic ailment. Whenever pus, blood, and other discharges are copious, and the wound is slow to close, it is especially important to replenish and nurture, ensuring that qi and blood recover. Otherwise, he may develop other conditions that will be difficult to treat; caution is advised!

Another man experienced toxins in his waist that manifested but did not break, with qi and blood being stagnated without the ability to turn into pus. After a few doses of potent tonics, the area finally erupted. Following several more doses, the pus remained clear. He then consumed a mixture of Ren, Qi, and Gui Zhi preparations, resulting in less viscous pus. Gradually, the pus became thicker, and muscle tissue began to form. In cases of large boils and abscesses, the condition primarily relies on qi. If an affliction arises without eruption or if it ruptures without rotting or fails to congeal—with pus being minimal or clear—it indicates a deficiency in qi and blood. Therefore, it warrants significant tonification while strictly avoiding aggressive medications. There are cases where pus reverts to being copious, indicating that the deficiency in qi and blood prevents control. If, after rupture, one experiences fever and thirst with a strong pulse and increasing pus, it pertains to genuine qi deficiency with excess pathogenic influence and will not heal effectively.

It is common to see robust individuals with conditions that lead to swollen, red lesions which easily rot and have viscous pus, making them easier to congeal. In contrast, weaker people often do not erupt, rot, or close easily. Should one recklessly administer aggressive treatments without careful examination, the risk of collapse and other complications becomes inevitable. After suffering from such conditions, one must focus on recovery, especially in cases resembling nodular or exudative ailments, where nourishment is particularly critical. Otherwise, one may develop additional complications that will be difficult to treat; caution is advised![134p]

　　佥宪张碧崖腰患疽，醉而入房，脉洪数，两尺更大，予辞不治。将登舟，其子强留，顷间吐臭血五六碗。予意此肾经虚火而血妄行，血必从齿缝出，合肉桂等补肾制火之药，各用罐煎熟听用，血止，拭齿视之，果然。遂与一锺冷服之，热渴顿止。少顷，温服一锺，脉细如脱，气息奄奄，得药则脉少复，良久仍脱。其子疑内有脓，欲刺之。予曰：必无。乃以鹅翎管纴内，果如予言。次日脉脱，脚寒至膝，腹内如冰，急用六君加姜、附，腹始温，脓始溃，疮口将完。彼因侍者皆爱妾，又患小便不通，此阴已痿而思色以降其精，精内败不出而然耳。用加减八味丸料，加参、芪、白朮一剂，小便虽愈，疮口不敛而殁。[135p]

The official Zhang Biyai suffered from a carbuncle at his waist. He entered the room inebriated, with a pulse that was rapid and strong, and the pain intensified. I advised against treatment. As he was about to board a boat, his son insisted he stay, and shortly thereafter he vomited foul-smelling blood, five or six bowls' worth. I suspected that this was due to deficiency in the kidney channel leading to chaotic blood flow; the blood would inevitably escape through the gaps between his teeth. I decided to use herbs such as cinnamon to tonify the kidneys and restrain the fire, preparing them for use. Once the bleeding stopped, I wiped his teeth and confirmed my suspicion. I then gave him a dose of cold medicine, which immediately alleviated his thirst. After a while, I administered a dose of warm medicine; his pulse became weak and his breathing shallow. After receiving the medicine, his pulse improved slightly but eventually became weak again. His son, suspecting there might be pus inside, wanted to puncture it. I said there was surely none. In the end, with a goose feather, it was confirmed to be just as I had predicted. The next day, his pulse was weak, his feet cold up to the knees, and his abdomen felt as if it were made of ice. I urgently applied a remedy of Six Gentleman Pills with ginger and Aconite, which warmed the abdomen and led to the beginning of pus discharge, with the sore seemingly healing. Since the attendants all loved his concubine, he also suffered from urinary obstruction; his yin was weak and sought release of essence, but the essence within had deteriorated and could not escape. I administered a modified version of the Eight Flavor Pill, adding ginseng, astragalus, and white atractylodes. Although his urination improved, the wound did not close and he eventually perished.[135p]

　　府庠彭碧溪患腰疽，服寒凉败毒之药，色黯不痛，疮头如铺黍，背重不能安寝，耳聩目白，面色无神，小便频濇，作渴迷闷，气粗短促，脉浮数，重按如无。予先用滋肾水之药一剂，少顷便利渴止，背即轻爽，乃砭去瘀血，以艾半斤许明灸患处，外傅乌金膏，内服参、芪、归、朮、肉桂等药，至数剂，元气稍复。自疑肉桂辛热，一日不用，手足并冷，大便不禁，仍加肉桂及补骨脂二钱、肉豆蔻一钱，大便如常，其肉渐溃，更用当归膏以生肌肉，八珍汤以补气血而愈。[136p]

The official from the prefectural school, Peng Bixi, suffered from a腰疽 (a type of sore). He took cold, detoxifying medicine, yet his complexion was dark and without pain, the sore resembling a layer of millet. He felt heavy in the back and could not sleep, his hearing was diminished, his eyesight cloudy, and his face lacked vitality. He experienced frequent, difficult urination, thirst, and a sense of confusion. His breathing was coarse and shallow, with a rapid pulse that felt faint under pressure.

I initially prescribed a remedy to nourish the kidney water, and after a while, he felt relief from thirst and his back felt lighter. Then I used needles to remove the stagnant blood and applied about half a jin of mugwort for moxibustion on the affected area. I also applied a medicinal ointment and internally prescribed ginseng, astragalus, angelica, poria, and cinnamon. After several doses, his vital energy slightly recovered.

However, he doubted the warming properties of cinnamon and stopped using it for a day. Subsequently, his hands and feet became cold, and he could not maintain regular bowel movements. I then increased the dosage of cinnamon and added two qian of psoralen and one qian of nutmeg. His bowel movements returned to normal, but the sore began to fester. I then used angelica ointment to promote flesh regeneration and prescribed Eight Treasures Decoction to replenish his vital energy and blood, resulting in his recovery.[136p]

　　举人顾东溪久作渴，六月初患腰疽，不慎起居，疮溃尺许色黯败臭，小便如淋，唇裂舌刺，七月终，左尺洪数，左关浮濇。予谓先渴而患疽者，乃肾水干涸，虚火上灸，多致不起。然脓水败臭，色黯不痛，疮口张大，乃脾气败而肾水绝也。左尺洪数，肾无所生也。左关浮濇，肺克肝也。况当金旺之际，危殆速矣。二日后果殁。盖此证既发于外两月方殁者，乃元气虚不能收敛也。若豫为调补使气血无亏，亦有得生者。[137p]

The scholar Gu Dongxi had long suffered from thirst and, in early June, developed a sore on his waist. Due to carelessness in his daily activities, the wound festered, became about a foot in size, dark in color, and emitted a foul smell. His urination resembled dribbling, his lips cracked, and his tongue felt prickly. By the end of July, his left wrist pulse was rapid and strong, and the pulse at his left guan position was superficial and weak. I believed that the initial thirst followed by the sore indicated that the kidney's water had dried up, resulting in deficient fire rising upward, making recovery unlikely. The pus was foul-smelling, dark in color, and painless, with the wound wide open, indicating that the spleen's energy had deteriorated and kidney water was exhausted. The rapid and strong left wrist pulse signified the kidney's inability to produce anything. The weak and superficial left guan pulse indicated lung overacting on the liver. Furthermore, during this time of metal flourishing, the situation was perilous. Two days later, he indeed passed away. This condition, having manifested from external factors for two months before his death, showed that his original qi was too weak to consolidate itself. If timely regulation and nourishment had been provided to prevent depletion of his qi and blood, there might have been a chance for survival.[137p]

　　《医门法律》曰：张令施乃弟伤寒坏证，两腰偻废，卧床彻夜痛叫，百治不效，求诊于余。其脉亦平顺无患，其痛则比前大减。余曰：病非死证，但恐成废人矣。此证之可以转移处，全在痛如刀刺，尚有邪正互争之象。若全然不痛，则邪正混为一家，相安于无事矣。今痛觉大减，实有可虑，宜速治之。病者曰：此身既废，不如速死。余蹙额欲为救全而无治法，谛思良久，谓邪深入两腰，血脉久闭，不能复出，只有攻散一法。而邪入既久，正气全虚，攻之必不应。乃以桃仁承气汤多加肉桂、附子二大剂与服，服后即能强起，再仿前意为丸，服至旬余全安。此非前人之已试，乃一时之权宜也，然有自来矣。仲景于结胸证，有附子泻心汤一法，原是附子与大黄同用，但在上之证气多，故以此法泻心。然在下之证血多，独不可仿其意，而合桃仁、肉桂以散腰间之血结乎？后江古生乃弟伤寒两腰偻废痛楚，不劳思索，径用此法，二剂而愈。[138p]

The "Medical Gate Law" states: Zhang Ling's younger brother suffered from typhoid fever leading to severe symptoms, weakening both loins, causing him to lie in bed crying out in pain throughout the night. After many treatments failed, he sought a diagnosis from me. His pulse was steady and showed no signs of illness, yet his pain had significantly decreased compared to before. I said, "This illness is not fatal, but I fear he may become incapacitated." The key to this condition lies in the pain that feels like a stabbing, indicating a struggle between the pathogenic and vital forces. If there were no pain at all, the pathogenic and vital forces would merge into one, coexisting without issue. Now that the pain perception has greatly diminished, it is indeed concerning and requires prompt treatment. The patient responded, "Since my body is already weakened, it would be better to die quickly." I furrowed my brow, wanting to save him but lacking a treatment method. After contemplating for a long time, I concluded that the pathogen had deeply penetrated both loins, causing blood vessels to close off for a long time and preventing proper circulation. The only method left was to disperse it. However, since the pathogen had been present for so long and the vital energy was completely exhausted, any aggressive treatment would likely be ineffective. Thus, I prescribed a modified version of the Tao Ren Cheng Qi Decoction, adding a large dosage of cinnamon and aconite. After taking it, the patient was able to rise with strength. I then followed my earlier intention to form it into pills, and after taking them for ten days, he was completely well. This was not a method already tested by previous practitioners, but rather a timely adaptation; however, it had been effective in the past. In Zhang Zhongjing's treatment of chest blockage, there is a method using Aconite and Rhubarb, which originally combines these two ingredients. However, in cases with excess energy above, this method is used to drain the heart. In contrast, for cases with excessive blood below, one cannot simply emulate its intention and combine peach kernel and cinnamon to disperse the blood stasis in the loins, can one? Later, Jiang Gusheng, Zhang's younger brother, suffered from typhoid fever with similar symptoms, and without overthinking, he directly applied this method, recovering after just two doses.[138p]

　　《景岳全书》曰：余尝治一董翁者年逾六句，资禀素壮，因好饮火酒，以致湿热聚于太阳，忽病腰痛不可忍，至求自尽，其甚可知。余为诊之，则六脉洪滑之甚，且小水不通而膀胱胀急。遂以大分清饮倍加黄蘗、龙胆草，一剂而小水顿通，小水通而腰痛如失。若用丹溪不可用寒凉之言，鲜不误矣，是以不可执也。
[139p]

The "Complete Book of Jingyue" states: I once treated an old man named Dong, who was over sixty years old. He had a solid constitution but enjoyed drinking strong liquor, which caused damp heat to accumulate in his lower back. Suddenly, he suffered from unbearable waist pain and even sought to end his own life; it was indeed grave. Upon examination, I found his six pulses to be notably full and slippery, and his urine was not flowing, causing a distended and urgent bladder. Therefore, I prescribed a decoction of clear tea with a double dose of Huangbo and Longdancao. After one dose, his urine flowed freely, and the waist pain vanished as if it had never been. If using Danxi's approach, one should avoid the cold and cool remedies; otherwise, it would lead to mistakes. Thus, one must not be rigid in treatments.[139p]
